Let me trace through `test_wrapper_debug`:\n\n1. `wrap_with_comment` wraps execute to prepend \"/* My comment */\" to SQL\n2. `CaptureQueriesContext` captures queries via `queries_log`\n3. `list(Person.objects.all())` runs a query with the wrapper\n\nThe flow:\n- `execute(sql, params)` in `CursorDebugWrapper` is called with the ORIGINAL sql\n- `debug_sql()` context manager starts, captures the start time\n- `super().execute(sql, params)` → `CursorWrapper.execute(sql, params)` is called\n\n\n- This invokes `_execute_with_wrappers(sql, params, many=False, executor=self._execute)` where the wrapper transforms the executor to apply the comment prefix\n- The modified SQL with the comment gets executed, but `debug_sql()` logs the original unmodified SQL via `self.db.ops.last_executed_query(self.cursor, sql, params)`\n- Since `use_last_executed_query=True`, it retrieves what the cursor actually executed—which should be the SQL with the comment already {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_019kUoVAiXepi6j4gdBHfnrH","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"All tests pass. Here's a summary of what I found and fixed:\n\n## The Bug\n\nIn `django/db/backends/utils.py`, `CursorDebugWrapper` overrode `execute()` and `executemany()` to wrap them with `debug_sql()` for query logging. The problem: `debug_sql` was called with the **original** SQL before execute wrappers had a chance to modify it.\n\n**Execution flow (before fix):**\n1. `CursorDebugWrapper.execute(original_sql)` — debug logging starts with `original_sql`\n2. `super().execute(original_sql)` → `_execute_with_wrappers()` → wrapper modifies to `\"/* My comment */ original_sql\"`\n3. `_execute(\"/* My comment */ original_sql\")` actually executes against the DB\n4. `debug_sql` logs `original_sql` (without the comment) — **bug!**\n\n## The Fix\n\nMoved the debug logging from `execute()`/`executemany()` to `_execute()`/`_executemany()`. These inner methods are invoked at the end of the execute wrapper chain, so they receive the **fully-modified** SQL that was actually sent to the database.\n\n**Execution flow (after fix):**\n1. `execute(original_sql)` → (inherited from `CursorWrapper`) → `_execute_with_wrappers()`\n2. The problem: `debug_sql` was called with the **original** SQL before execute wrappers had a chance to modify it.\n\n**Execution flow (before fix):**\n1. `CursorDebugWrapper.execute(original_sql)` — debug logging starts with `original_sql`\n2. `super().execute(original_sql)` → `_execute_with_wrappers()` → wrapper modifies to `\"/* My comment */ original_sql\"`\n3. `_execute(\"/* My comment */ original_sql\")` actually executes against the DB\n4. `debug_sql` logs `original_sql` (without the comment) — **bug!**\n\n## The Fix\n\nMoved the debug logging from `execute()`/`executemany()` to `_execute()`/`_executemany()`. These inner methods are invoked at the end of the execute wrapper chain, so they receive the **fully-modified** SQL that was actually sent to the database.\n\n**Execution flow (after fix):**\n1. `execute(original_sql)` → (inherited from `CursorWrapper`) → `_execute_with_wrappers()`\n2.
